Once allocated, Types are never\\n43: /// free'd.\\n44: ///\\n45: class Type {\\n46: public:\\n47:   //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n48:   /// Definitions of all of the base types for the Type system.  Based on this\\n49:   /// value, you can cast to a class defined in DerivedTypes.h.\\n50:   /// Note: If you add an element to this, you need to add an element to the\\n51:   /// Type::getPrimitiveType function, or else things will break!\\n52:   /// Also update LLVMTypeKind and LLVMGetTypeKind () in the C binding.\\n53:   ///\\n54:   enum TypeID {\\n55:     // PrimitiveTypes\\n56:     HalfTyID = 0,  ///< 16-bit floating point type\\n57:     BFloatTyID,    ///< 16-bit floating point type (7-bit significand)\\n58:     FloatTyID,     ///< 32-bit floating point type\\n59:     DoubleTyID,    ///< 64-bit floating point type\\n60:     X86_FP80TyID,  ///< 80-bit floating point type (X87)\\n61:     FP128TyID,     ///< 128-bit floating point type (112-bit significand)\\n62:     PPC_FP128TyID, ///< 128-bit floating point type (two 64-bits, PowerPC)\\n63:     VoidTyID,      ///< type with no size\\n64:     LabelTyID,     ///< Labels\\n65:     MetadataTyID,  ///< Metadata\\n66:     X86_AMXTyID,   ///< AMX vectors (8192 bits, X86 specific)\\n67:     TokenTyID,     ///< Tokens\\n68: \\n69:     // Derived types... see DerivedTypes.h file.\\n70:     IntegerTyID,        ///< Arbitrary bit width integers\\n71:     FunctionTyID,       ///< Functions\\n72:     PointerTyID,        ///< Pointers\\n73:     StructTyID,         ///< Structures\\n74:     ArrayTyID,          ///< Arrays\\n75:     FixedVectorTyID,    ///< Fixed width SIMD vector type\\n76:     ScalableVectorTyID, ///< Scalable SIMD vector type\\n77:     TypedPointerTyID,   ///< Typed pointer used by some GPU targets\\n78:     TargetExtTyID,      ///< Target extension type\\n79:   };\\n80: \\n81: private:\\n82:   /// This refers to the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\\n83:   LLVMContext &Context;\\n84: \\n85:   TypeID   ID : 8;            // The current base type of this type.\\n86:   unsigned SubclassData : 24; // Space for subclasses to store data.\\n87:                               // Note that this should be synchronized with\\n88:                               // MAX_INT_BITS value in IntegerType class.\\n89: \\n90: protected:\\n91:   friend class LLVMContextImpl;\\n92: \\n93:   explicit Type(LLVMContext &C, TypeID tid)\\n94:     : Context(C), ID(tid), SubclassData(0) {}\\n95:   ~Type() = default;\\n96: \\n97:   unsigned getSubclassData() const { return SubclassData; }\\n98: \\n99:   void setSubclassData(unsigned val) {\\n100:     SubclassData = val;\\n101:     // Ensure we don't have any accidental truncation.\\n102:     assert(getSubclassData() == val && \\\"Subclass data too large for field\\\");\\n103:   }\\n104: \\n105:   /// Keeps track of how many Type*'s there are in the ContainedTys list.\\n106:   unsigned NumContainedTys = 0;\\n107: \\n108:   /// A pointer to the array of Types contained by this Type. For example, this\\n109:   /// includes the arguments of a function type, the elements of a structure,\\n110:   /// the pointee of a pointer, the element type of an array, etc. This pointer\\n111:   /// may be 0 for types that don't contain other types (Integer, Double,\\n112:   /// Float).\\n113:   Type * const *ContainedTys = nullptr;\\n114: \\n115: public:\\n116:   /// Print the current type.\\n117:   /// Omit the type details if \\\\p NoDetails == true.\\n118:   /// E.g., let %st = type { i32, i16 }\\n119:   /// When \\\\p NoDetails is true, we only print %st.\\n120:   /// Put differently, \\\\p NoDetails prints the type as if\\n121:   /// inlined with the operands when printing an instruction.\\n122:   LLVM_ABI void print(raw_ostream &O, bool IsForDebug = false,\\n123:                       bool NoDetails = false) const;\\n124: \\n125:   LLVM_ABI void dump() const;\\n126: \\n127:   /// Return the LLVMContext in which this type was uniqued.\\n128:   LLVMContext &getContext() const { return Context; }\\n129: \\n130:   //===--------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n131:   // Accessors for working with types.\\n132:   //\\n133: \\n134:   /// Return the type id for the type. This will return one of the TypeID enum\\n135:   /// elements defined above.\\n136:   TypeID getTypeID() const { return ID; }\\n137: \\n138:   /// Return true if this is 'void'.\\n139:   bool isVoidTy() const { return getTypeID() == VoidTyID; }\\n140: \\n141:   /// Return true if this is 'half', a 16-bit IEEE fp type.\\n142:   bool isHalfTy() const { return getTypeID() == HalfTyID; }\\n143: \\n144:   /// Return true if this is 'bfloat', a 16-bit bfloat type.\\n145:   bool isBFloatTy() const { return getTypeID() == BFloatTyID; }\\n146: \\n147:   /// Return true if this is a 16-bit float type.\\n148:   bool is16bitFPTy() const {\\n149:     return getTypeID() == BFloatTyID || getTypeID() == HalfTyID;\\n150:   }\\n151: \\n152:   /// Return true if this is 'float', a 32-bit IEEE fp type.\\n153:   bool isFloatTy() const { return getTypeID() == FloatTyID; }\\n160: \\n161:   /// Return true if this is 'fp128'.\\n162:   bool isFP128Ty() const { return getTypeID() == FP128TyID; }\\n163: \\n164:   /// Return true if this is powerpc long double.\\n165:   bool isPPC_FP128Ty() const { return getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID; }\\n166: \\n167:   /// Return true if this is a well-behaved IEEE-like type, which has a IEEE\\n168:   /// compatible layout, and does not have non-IEEE values, such as x86_fp80's\\n169:   /// unnormal values.\\n170:   bool isIEEELikeFPTy() const {\\n171:     switch (getTypeID()) {\\n172:     case DoubleTyID:\\n173:     case FloatTyID:\\n174:     case HalfTyID:\\n175:     case BFloatTyID:\\n176:     case FP128TyID:\\n177:       return true;\\n178:     default:\\n179:       return false;\\n180:     }\\n181:   }\\n182: \\n183:   /// Return true if this is one of the floating-point types\\n184:   bool isFloatingPointTy() const {\\n185:     return isIEEELikeFPTy() || getTypeID() == X86_FP80TyID ||\\n186:            getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID;\\n187:   }\\n188: \\n189:   /// Returns true if this is a floating-point type that is an unevaluated sum\\n190:   /// of multiple floating-point units.\\n191:   /// An example of such a type is ppc_fp128, also known as double-double, which\\n192:   /// consists of two IEEE 754 doubles.\\n193:   bool isMultiUnitFPType() const {\\n194:     return getTypeID() == PPC_FP128TyID;\\n195:   }\\n196: \\n197:   LLVM_ABI const fltSemantics &getFltSemantics() const;\\n198: \\n199:   /// Return true if this is X86 AMX.\\n200:   bool isX86_AMXTy() const { return getTypeID() == X86_AMXTyID; System to Code Generation Chain\\n\\n## Overview\\nThe LLVM IR type system flows through several layers from creation to machine code generation. This trace documents the complete chain of how LLVM IR types are created, managed, and converted to machine value types in SelectionDAG for code generation.\\n\\n## 1. Type Class Hierarchy\\n\\n### Base Type Class (llvm/include/llvm/IR/Type.h)\\nThe `Type` class is the base class for all LLVM IR types. It defines a TypeID enum with all type categories (primitive types like VoidTyID, FloatTyID, and derived types like IntegerTyID, FunctionTyID, StructTyID, etc.). The Type class maintains:\\n- A reference to the LLVMContext in which it was created (line 82-83)\\n- Type ID and subclass data fields (line 85-86)\\n- An array of contained types for composite types (line 106-113)\\n\\nKey features:\\n- Types are immutable and uniqued (only one instance of each type)\\n- Type instances are never freed after creation\\n- Equality checking is done via pointer comparison\\n\\n### Derived Type Classes (llvm/include/llvm/IR/DerivedTypes.h)\\n\\n**IntegerType (line 42-97)**:\\n- Represents arbitrary bit-width integer types\\n- Created via `IntegerType::get(LLVMContext &C, unsigned NumBits)` (line 66)\\n- Stores bit width in subclass data (24-bit field)\\n- Minimum 1 bit, maximum 8,388,608 bits\\n\\n**FunctionType (line 105-150)**:\\n- Represents function signatures\\n- Created via `FunctionType::get(Type *Result, ArrayRef<Type *> Params, bool isVarArg)` (line 113-114)\\n- Contains return type as first element in ContainedTys array\\n- Parameter types follow the return type\\n- Stores vararg flag in subclass data\\n\\n**StructType (line 218-301)**:\\n- Represents structure types, both literal and identified\\n- Literal structs are uniqued structurally via `get()` methods (line 265-269)\\n- Identified structs created via `create()` methods (line 246-256)\\n- Can be opaque (no body specified yet) or have body\\n- Supports named and unnamed structs\\n- Stores flags: HasBody, Packed, IsLiteral, IsSized in subclass data\\n\\n## 2. Type Creation API and Context Ownership\\n\\n### Type Creation Factories (llvm/lib/IR/Type.cpp, lines 279-340)\\n\\nPrimitive types are created and cached in LLVMContext:\\n```cpp\\nType *Type::getVoidTy(LLVMContext &C) { return &C.pImpl->VoidTy; }\\nIntegerType *Type::getInt32Ty(LLVMContext &C) { return &C.pImpl->Int32Ty; }\\nIntegerType *Type::getInt64Ty(LLVMContext &C) { return &C.pImpl->Int64Ty; }\\nIntegerType *Type::getIntNTy(LLVMContext &C, unsigned N) { return IntegerType::get(C, N); }\\n```\\n\\nCustom integer types use the context's type cache:\\n```cpp\\nIntegerType *IntegerType::get(LLVMContext &C, unsigned NumBits) {\\n  // Built-in types (1, 8, 16, 32, 64, 128) cached directly in context\\n  // Custom types stored in C.pImpl->IntegerTypes[NumBits]\\n  // Allocation happens in context's bump allocator\\n}\\n```\\n\\n### Context Ownership (llvm/lib/IR/LLVMContextImpl.h, lines 1758-1768)\\n\\nLLVMContextImpl stores all types for a context:\\n```cpp\\nDenseMap<unsigned, IntegerType *> IntegerTypes;  // Custom integer type cache\\nusing FunctionTypeSet = DenseSet<FunctionType *, FunctionTypeKeyInfo>;\\nFunctionTypeSet FunctionTypes;  // Function type uniquing cache\\nusing StructTypeSet = DenseSet<StructType *, AnonStructTypeKeyInfo>;\\nStructTypeSet AnonStructTypes;  // Anonymous struct uniquing\\nStringMap<StructType *> NamedStructTypes;  // Named struct registry\\n```\\n\\nType uniquing is enforced through:\\n- **KeyInfo structures** that define equality and hashing:\\n  - `AnonStructTypeKeyInfo` (line 93-138): Hashes on element types and packed flag\\n  - `FunctionTypeKeyInfo` (line 140-190): Hashes on return type, parameters, vararg flag\\n- **DenseSet/DenseMap containers** that ensure only one instance per unique type exists\\n- **LLVMContext allocator** (BumpPtrAllocator in pImpl) for all type allocations\\n\\n## 3. SelectionDAG Type Lowering Pipeline\\n\\n### Step 1: IR Type to EVT Conversion\\n\\n**Location**: llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/TargetLowering.h (lines 1740-1758)\\n\\n`TargetLowering::getValueType()` is the primary gateway converting LLVM IR types to Extended Value Types (EVTs):\\n\\n```cpp\\nEVT getValueType(const DataLayout &DL, Type *Ty, bool AllowUnknown = false) const {\\n  // Handle pointers specially - convert to native pointer types\\n  if (auto *PTy = dyn_cast<PointerType>(Ty))\\n    return getPointerTy(DL, PTy->getAddressSpace());\\n  \\n  // Handle vectors of types\\n  if (auto *VTy = dyn_cast<VectorType>(Ty)) {\\n    EVT EltVT = EVT::getEVT(VTy->getElementType(), false);\\n    return EVT::getVectorVT(Ty->getContext(), EltVT, VTy->getElementCount());\\n  }\\n  \\n  // Default conversion for scalar types\\n  return EVT::getEVT(Ty, AllowUnknown);\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThis method is called during SelectionDAGBuilder in llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAGBuilder.cpp (line 2276):\\n```cpp\\nfor (unsigned j = 0; j != NumValues; ++j) {\\n  EVT VT = TLI.getValueType(DL, Types[j]);  // Converts Type* to EVT\\n  MVT PartVT = TLI.getRegisterTypeForCallingConv(Context, CC, VT);\\n}\\n```\\n\\n### Step 2: EVT Structure (llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/ValueTypes.h, lines 35-150)\\n\\n**EVT (Extended Value Type)** holds both simple and extended types:\\n```cpp\\nstruct EVT {\\nprivate:\\n  MVT V = MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE;  // Simple value type (i1, i8, i32, f64, etc.)\\n  Type *LLVMTy = nullptr;  // LLVM IR Type* for extended types\\n\\npublic:\\n  // Static factory methods for type construction\\n  static EVT getIntegerVT(LLVMContext &Context, unsigned BitWidth);\\n  static EVT getVectorVT(LLVMContext &Context, EVT VT, unsigned NumElements);\\n  static EVT getEVT(Type *Ty, bool HandleUnknown = false);  // Creates from LLVM Type\\n}\\n```\\n\\n**EVT::getEVT()** conversion (line 510):\\n- For types representable as MVT (simple types): Returns MVT wrapped in EVT\\n- For extended types (non-power-of-2 integers, structures, etc.): Stores LLVM Type* in LLVMTy field\\n- Enables representation of arbitrary-width integers and complex types in SelectionDAG\\n\\n### Step 3: SelectionDAG Type Legalization\\n\\n**Location**: llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeTypes.cpp\\n\\nThe `DAGTypeLegalizer` class handles type legalization by transforming non-legal EVTs to legal ones:\\n\\n```cpp\\n// Example from LegalizeTypesGeneric.cpp (line 254)\\nEVT ValueVT = LD->getValueType(0);  // Get EVT from load\\nEVT NVT = TLI.getTypeToTransformTo(*DAG.getContext(), ValueVT);  // Transform to legal type\\n```\\n\\nType legalization strategies:\\n1. **Promotion**: Illegal type → larger legal type (e.g., i8 → i32)\\n2. **Expansion**: Illegal type → multiple smaller legal types (e.g., i64 → 2×i32)\\n3. **Splitting**: Vector type → smaller vectors\\n4. **Scalarization**: Vector → scalars\\n5. **Softening**: Float → integer operations via libcalls\\n\\n### Step 4: Machine Type Lowering\\n\\n**TargetLowering type tables** define legal machine types:\\n\\n```cpp\\n// From TargetLowering.h (line 1791-1794)\\nMVT getRegisterType(MVT VT) const {\\n  return RegisterTypeForVT[VT.SimpleTy];  // Maps VT to register type\\n}\\n```\\n\\nTarget subclasses override type action tables:\\n- `ValueTypeActions`: Maps EVT → legal action (Promote/Expand/LibCall/etc.)\\n- `RegisterTypeForVT`: Maps MVT → register type\\n- `NumRegistersForVT`: Maps MVT → number of registers needed\\n\\n## 4. SelectionDAG Node Type System\\n\\n**Location**: llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/SelectionDAG.h, llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/SelectionDAG.cpp\\n\\nSelectionDAG nodes use EVT to track value types:\\n- Each SDNode has value types in SDVTList\\n- SDValue wraps (SDNode*, ResNo) and provides `.getValueType()` returning EVT\\n- Type information flows through DAG optimization and legalization passes\\n\\nSelectionDAG provides EVT-aware helpers:\\n```cpp\\nSDValue getValueType(EVT);  // Creates constant SDNode with type value\\nEVT getEVTAlign(EVT VT);    // Converts EVT to alignment\\n```\\n\\n## 5. Complete Flow Example\\n\\nFor a function parameter of type `i32`:\\n\\n1. **IR Level**: `Type::getInt32Ty(Context)` returns cached IntegerType instance\\n2. **Context Ownership**: Stored in `Context.pImpl->Int32Ty`\\n3. **SelectionDAGBuilder**: Calls `TLI.getValueType(DL, Type::getInt32Ty(...))`\\n4. **EVT Creation**: `EVT::getEVT()` returns MVT::i32 wrapped in EVT\\n5. **Legalization**: LegalizeTypes checks if i32 is legal (typically yes)\\n6. **RegisterTypes**: TargetLowering maps i32 → GPR type (e.g., MVT::i64 on 64-bit targets)\\n7. **Code Generation**: SelectionDAG uses EVT through all DAG combines, lowering, and ISel\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n1. **Type Uniquing**: All types are uniqued in LLVMContext, enabling pointer comparison\\n2. **Context Ownership**: All types belong to a single LLVMContext lifetime\\n3. **Immutability**: Types are immutable after creation (thread-safe)\\n4. **Lazy Legalization**: Types are only legalized when needed during SelectionDAG processing\\n5. **Target-Aware Lowering**: TargetLowering translates IR types to target-specific machine types\\n6. **Extended Value Types**: EVT bridges LLVM IR types and machine value types for arbitrary-width types\\n\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":7,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3058,"cache_read_input_tokens":109943,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3058},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"1afb8446-494d-44cd-b54e-199e8b3b3ad1","uuid":"2901cf44-fe5b-4c3d-b354-b28df4742490"}

Type Class Hierarchy\\n\\n### Base Type Class (llvm/include/llvm/IR/Type.h)\\nThe `Type` class is the base class for all LLVM IR types. Complete Flow Example\\n\\nFor a function parameter of type `i32`:\\n\\n1. **IR Level**: `Type::getInt32Ty(Context)` returns cached IntegerType instance\\n2. **Context Ownership**: Stored in `Context.pImpl->Int32Ty`\\n3. **SelectionDAGBuilder**: Calls `TLI.getValueType(DL, Type::getInt32Ty(...))`\\n4. **EVT Creation**: `EVT::getEVT()` returns MVT::i32 wrapped in EVT\\n5. **Legalization**: LegalizeTypes checks if i32 is legal (typically yes)\\n6. **RegisterTypes**: TargetLowering maps i32 → GPR type (e.g., MVT::i64 on 64-bit targets)\\n7. **Code Generation**: SelectionDAG uses EVT through all DAG combines, lowering, and ISel\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n1. **Type Uniquing**: All types are uniqued in LLVMContext, enabling pointer comparison\\n2. **Context Ownership**: All types belong to a single LLVMContext lifetime\\n3. **Immutability**: Types are immutable after creation (thread-safe)\\n4. **Lazy Legalization**: Types are only legalized when needed during SelectionDAG processing\\n5. **Target-Aware Lowering**: TargetLowering translates IR types to target-specific machine types\\n6. **Extended Value Types**: EVT bridges LLVM IR types and machine value types for arbitrary-width types\\n\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
